## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position, velocity, and time. The acceleration is governed by restoring forces (functions of x) and possibly damping forces (functions of v), characteristic of nonlinear oscillator equations of motion.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring force plus linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring force with damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Forced nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (Duffing with periodic driving)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity-dependent damping)
- Cubic damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity damping)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (mixed coupling term)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power restoring forces (x**2) → asymmetric potential wells causing drift or asymmetric oscillation
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v → linear energy dissipation or injection
- Terms like (1 - x**2)*v → amplitude-dependent damping switching from negative to positive damping (self-sustained oscillations)
- Cubic position terms (x**3) → Duffing-type hardening (positive coefficient) or softening (negative coefficient) spring behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous/conservative or dissipative system; presence of sin/cos(t) → externally driven system
- Products x*v or x**2*v → nonlinear energy exchange between kinetic and potential modes
- Sign of linear x coefficient determines oscillatory (negative) vs unstable (positive) equilibrium behavior

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT:** `-0.493165631499977*v*(1 - x**2) - 1.16769962902767*x*exp(-Abs(x))`

Expanding: `0.493165631499977*v*x**2 - 0.493165631499977*v - 1.16769962902767*x*exp(-Abs(x))`

The GT has three basis function components:
1. `v*x**2` (coefficient ≈ 0.493)
2. `v` (coefficient ≈ -0.493)
3. `x*exp(-|x|)` (coefficient ≈ -1.168)

The key challenge is matching `x*exp(-|x|)`. Note that `|x|` means this is NOT simply `x*exp(-x)` or `x*exp(x)`. For x > 0, it's `x*exp(-x)`, and for x < 0, it's `x*exp(x)`.

Let me check if any candidate basis functions can represent `x*exp(-|x|)`:

- `x*exp(c*x²)`: This is an even-in-exponent function. `exp(-|x|) ≠ exp(c*x²)` for any c.
- `sin(x)`, `cos(x)`: Periodic, can't match exponential decay.
- `x**c` (power law): Can't match exponential decay.
- `x*log(c*x²+1)`: Not exponential decay.
- `log(c*exp(c*x)+1)`: Softplus-like, not `x*exp(-|x|)`.
- `exp(c*x²)*sin(c*x)`: This is even in x² but odd via sin - interesting but not `x*exp(-|x|)`.
- `x**3`, `x**5`: Polynomials, can't match.

The function `x*exp(-|x|)` is a very specific non-analytic function (has a kink at x=0). None of the candidate basis functions can exactly reproduce it:

- `x*exp(c*x²)` with c < 0 gives Gaussian-like decay, not exponential decay
- No combination of polynomials, trigonometric functions, logarithms, or Gaussian-type functions can exactly equal `x*exp(-|x|)`
- `log(c*exp(c*x)+1)` is a softplus, which is smooth and cannot reproduce `exp(-|x|)`

Since `x*exp(-|x|)` involves `|x|` which creates a non-analytic point at x=0, and none of the candidates contain `Abs(x)` in their exponential terms (they use `x²` which is smooth), none can exactly match.

Let me verify: Could any combination of terms accidentally produce `x*exp(-|x|)`? The candidates use basis functions like `x*exp(c*x²)`, `sin(x)`, `x**n`, `log(...)`, etc. These are all analytic functions (smooth everywhere). But `x*exp(-|x|)` has a discontinuous second derivative at x=0. No finite sum of analytic functions can produce a non-analytic function.

Therefore, **no candidate can exactly match the GT**.

Let me do a quick sanity check on each candidate - they all lack `Abs(x)` or `exp(-|x|)` terms, confirming no match is possible.
